    \includegraphics{images/dct_dict.png}

    \hypertarget{orthogonal-matching-pursuit-omp-the-greedy-strategy}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{4.1 Orthogonal Matching Pursuit
(OMP): The Greedy
Strategy}}{4.1 Orthogonal Matching Pursuit (OMP): The Greedy Strategy}}\label{orthogonal-matching-pursuit-omp-the-greedy-strategy}}

OMP builds up the active set of dictionary atoms incrementally. It
iteratively selects dictionary atoms that best correlate with the
current residual. At iteration \(t\):

\textbf{Initialization} *
\(\mathbf{r}_0 = \mathbf{x}, \quad S_0 = \emptyset\) * \(\mathbf{r}_t\)
is the residual --- the part of \(\mathbf{x}\) not yet explained by the
chosen atoms, and \(S_t\) is the active set.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Atom Selection}

Find atom with maximum correlation: select the dictionary atom
\(\mathbf{d}_k\) that has the highest absolute correlation with the
current residual:
\(k_t = \underset{k}{\arg\max} |\langle \mathbf{d}_k, \mathbf{r}_{t-1} \rangle|\).
Intuitively, we pick the atom that best aligns (in direction) with what
remains unexplained in the signal.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Active Set Update}

Add this atom index to the active set: \(S_t = S_{t-1} \cup {k_t}\)

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Coefficient Update (Orthogonal Projection)}

Solve a \textbf{least-squares problem} over all selected atoms to
compute the optimal coefficients:
\(\boldsymbol{\alpha}_t = \underset{{\boldsymbol{\alpha}_{S_t}}}{\arg\min} \|\mathbf{x} - \mathbf{D}_{S_t}\boldsymbol{\alpha}_{S_t}\|_2^2\).
Analytically:
\(\boldsymbol{\alpha}_t = (\mathbf{D}_{S_t}^T\mathbf{D}_{S_t})^{-1}\mathbf{D}_{S_t}^T \mathbf{x}\).
This step makes OMP \textbf{orthogonal} --- unlike basic Matching
Pursuit (MP), OMP re-orthogonalizes the residual against all selected
atoms.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Residual Update}

\(\mathbf{r}_t = \mathbf{x} - \mathbf{D}_{S_t}\boldsymbol{\alpha}_t\).
The residual is now orthogonal to all selected atoms:
\(\mathbf{D}_{S_t}^T \mathbf{r}_t = 0\). This orthogonality ensures
convergence and stability.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Stopping Criteria}

Stop if:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  The residual energy is small enough: \(\|\mathbf{r}_t\|_2 < \tau\)
\item
  or the maximum number of coefficients \(t_{\max}\) is reached,
\item
  or the maximum correlation \(r_{c,\max}\) drops below threshold.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{the-omp-algorithm}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{The OMP
Algorithm}}{The OMP Algorithm}}\label{the-omp-algorithm}}

\(\boxed{ \begin{aligned} &\textbf{Initialize:}\quad \mathbf{r}_0 = \mathbf{x},\quad S_0 = \emptyset \\[4pt] &\textbf{For } t = 1, 2, \ldots \\[4pt] &\quad k_t = \arg\max_{k}\, |\langle \mathbf{d}_k,\; \mathbf{r}_{t-1} \rangle| \\[6pt] &\quad S_t = S_{t-1} \cup \{k_t\} \\[6pt] &\quad \boldsymbol{\alpha}_t  = \arg\min_{\boldsymbol{\alpha}}  \|\mathbf{x} - \mathbf{D}_{S_t}\boldsymbol{\alpha}\|_2^{2} \\[6pt] &\quad \mathbf{r}_t = \mathbf{x} - \mathbf{D}_{S_t}\,\boldsymbol{\alpha}_t \\[6pt] &\textbf{End if}\quad \|\mathbf{r}_t\|_2 < \tau \end{aligned} }\)

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Why OMP Works Well for Denoising \& Inpainting}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Sparse priors are \textbf{nonlinear filters} that preserve edges and
  textures while removing noise.
\item
  Inpainting uses \textbf{partial observation OMP}, where only known
  pixels contribute to the residual.
\item
  Overlapping patches ensure \textbf{smooth transitions} across
  boundaries.
\item
  DCT or Haar bases provide \textbf{multi-scale and frequency-localized
  atoms} --- excellent for natural images.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Limitations}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Computationally expensive for large images.
\item
  Fixed dictionaries (DCT/Haar) may not adapt to all image types.
\item
  Greedy pursuit may not achieve global optimum (compared to convex L1
  methods like LASSO).
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Connections to Other Sparse Optimization Techniques}

\includegraphics{images/spopt.png}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

Orthogonal Matching Pursuit bridges \textbf{theory and practice} in
sparse image modeling:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  It provides a clear geometric interpretation --- sequentially
  projecting onto subspaces spanned by dictionary atoms.
\item
  It enables practical algorithms for \textbf{denoising},
  \textbf{inpainting}, and \textbf{compression}.
\item
  It serves as a conceptual link to more advanced iterative methods like
  \textbf{ISTA}, \textbf{FISTA}, and \textbf{ADMM}, discussed in earlier
  sections.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{inpainting-image-inpainting-with-sparse-representations-omp}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{4.2 Inpainting Image Inpainting
with Sparse Representations
(OMP)}}{4.2 Inpainting Image Inpainting with Sparse Representations (OMP)}}\label{inpainting-image-inpainting-with-sparse-representations-omp}}

Inpainting reconstructs missing pixels based on known pixels and sparse
priors. Let \(\mathbf{M}\) be a binary mask (\(1\) = known pixel, \(0\)
= missing). We aim to find coefficients \(\boldsymbol{\alpha}\) such
that:
\(\underset{\boldsymbol{\alpha}}{\min} \| \mathbf{M} \odot (\mathbf{x} - \mathbf{D}\boldsymbol{\alpha}) \|_2^2 + \lambda \|\boldsymbol{\alpha}\|_0\).
This is solved patch-by-patch using OMP, considering only known pixels
in each patch. Under the hood:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{overlap\_im2col()} extracts overlapping patches.
\item
  \texttt{OMP\_Inpainting()} runs OMP on masked data.
\item
  \texttt{overlap\_col2im()} aggregates reconstructed patches back into
  the image.
\end{itemize}

This yields a smooth, natural reconstruction even for large missing
regions (e.g., text removal, scratch filling), as demonstrated using the
next code snippet.

    \begin{tcolorbox}[breakable, size=fbox, boxrule=1pt, pad at break*=1mm,colback=cellbackground, colframe=cellborder]
\prompt{In}{incolor}{ }{\boxspacing}
\begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
\PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} https://github.com/chongyangtao/Color\PYZhy{}Image\PYZhy{}Inpainting}
\PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} https://www.chegg.com/homework\PYZhy{}help/questions\PYZhy{}and\PYZhy{}answers/kercise\PYZhy{}8\PYZhy{}inpainting\PYZhy{}plement\PYZhy{}method\PYZhy{}solving\PYZhy{}inpainting\PYZhy{}problem\PYZhy{}region\PYZhy{}d\PYZhy{}subset\PYZhy{}omega\PYZhy{}unkno\PYZhy{}q100507908}
\PY{k+kn}{from}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nn}{scipy}\PY{n+nn}{.}\PY{n+nn}{sparse}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{k+kn}{import} \PY{n}{dok\PYZus{}matrix} \PY{k}{as} \PY{n}{sparse}
\PY{k+kn}{from}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nn}{scipy}\PY{n+nn}{.}\PY{n+nn}{sparse}\PY{n+nn}{.}\PY{n+nn}{linalg}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{k+kn}{import} \PY{n}{lsqr}

\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{overlap\PYZus{}col2im}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{X}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{Mask}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{overlap}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{im\PYZus{}size}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Get image dimensions}
    \PY{n}{M}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{N} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{im\PYZus{}size}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Initialise the image}
    \PY{n}{I} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{zeros}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{M}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{N}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Initialise the matrix that stores the cubetalative signal used to calculate each pixel}
    \PY{n}{S} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{zeros}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{M}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{N}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Calculate how many patches fit horisontally and vertically}
    \PY{n}{row} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{M} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{/}\PY{o}{/}\PY{n}{overlap}
    \PY{n}{col} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{N} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{/}\PY{o}{/}\PY{n}{overlap}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Iterate through patches and keep a counter to know what column of X to access next}
    \PY{n}{counter} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{row}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{col}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:} 
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Get x and y range of current patch}
            \PY{n}{x\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{y\PYZus{}patch} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{arange}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{i}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{overlap}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{arange}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{j}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{overlap}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Get existing patch}
            \PY{n}{existing\PYZus{}patch} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{x\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{y\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Get current patch and calculate its signal strength}
            \PY{n}{current\PYZus{}patch} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{reshape}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{X}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{counter}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
            \PY{n}{signal} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{sum}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{Mask}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{counter}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{!=}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{)}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Update cubetalative signal strength}
            \PY{n}{S}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{x\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{y\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{+}\PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{signal}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Update patch}
            \PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{x\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{y\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{existing\PYZus{}patch} \PY{o}{+} \PY{n}{current\PYZus{}patch}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{signal}
            \PY{n}{counter} \PY{o}{+}\PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}S = S / S.max()}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} If a pixel was not covered by a single patch with signal, set its signal}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} value to 1, in order to prevent division by zero}
    \PY{n}{S}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{S} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Divide each pixel by its corresponding cubetalative signal coverage}
    \PY{n}{I} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{I} \PY{o}{/} \PY{n}{S}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{I}

\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{OMP\PYZus{}Inpainting}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{D}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{X}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{Mask}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{sigma}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}min}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{max\PYZus{}coeff}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}    
    \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{P} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{X}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} 64 * 552108}
    \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{K} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{D}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}
    \PY{n}{A} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{sparse}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{D}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{X}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{k} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{P}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{n}{Mpos} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{nonzero}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{Mask}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{k}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}
        \PY{n}{indx} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{]}
        \PY{k}{if} \PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{Mpos}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n}{Dict} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{D}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{Mpos}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}W = 1/np.sqrt(np.diag(Dict.T@Dict))}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}Dict = Dict@np.diag(W)}
            \PY{n}{x} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{X}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{Mpos}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{k}\PY{p}{]} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} patch exclude mask}
            \PY{n}{residual}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{a} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{x}\PY{p}{,} \PY{k+kc}{None}
            \PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}max} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{inf}
            \PY{n}{threshold} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{linalg}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{norm}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{x}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{sigma}
            \PY{n}{DD} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{array}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)} 
            \PY{k}{while} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{linalg}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{norm}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{residual}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{n}{threshold} \PY{o+ow}{and} \PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}max} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}min} \PY{o+ow}{and} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{sum}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{a}\PY{o}{!=}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{\PYZlt{}} \PY{n}{max\PYZus{}coeff}\PY{p}{:}
                \PY{n}{proj} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{abs}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{Dict}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{T}\PY{n+nd}{@residual}\PY{p}{)}
                \PY{n}{pos} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{argmax}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{proj}\PY{p}{)}
                \PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}max} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{proj}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{pos}\PY{p}{]}
                \PY{n}{DD} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{Dict}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{pos}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{reshape}\PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)} \PY{k}{if} \PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{DD}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+m+mi}{0} \PY{k}{else} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{hstack}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{DD}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{Dict}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{pos}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{reshape}\PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
                \PY{n}{indx}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{append}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{pos}\PY{p}{)}
                \PY{n}{a} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{lsqr}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{DD}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{x}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}
                \PY{n}{residual} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{x} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n}{DD}\PY{n+nd}{@a}
                \PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{+}\PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}                       
        \PY{k}{if} \PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{indx}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n}{A}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{indx}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{k}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{a}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}A[:,k]=W*A[:,k]            }
        \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{k} \PY{o}{\PYZpc{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1000} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n+nb}{print}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+sa}{f}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{iter:  }\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZob{}}\PY{n}{k}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZcb{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{/}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZob{}}\PY{n}{P}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZcb{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{ | (\PYZpc{}}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZob{}}\PY{n}{k}\PY{o}{/}\PY{n}{P}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZcb{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZpc{}\PYZpc{})}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{A}

\PY{n}{bb} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{8}
\PY{n}{K} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{16}
\PY{n}{D} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{get\PYZus{}dct\PYZus{}dictionary}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{K}\PY{p}{)}
\PY{n}{im} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{cv2}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{imread}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{images/lena256.jpg}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{)}

\PY{n}{im} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{im} \PY{o}{/} \PY{n}{im}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{max}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}
\PY{n}{M}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{N} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{im}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}
\PY{n}{overlap} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{3}
        
\PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}Compute mask and extracting its patches}
\PY{n}{mask} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{img\PYZus{}mask} \PY{o}{\PYZlt{}} \PY{l+m+mf}{0.3}\PY{p}{)}
\PY{n}{blk\PYZus{}mask} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{overlap\PYZus{}im2col}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{mask}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{overlap}\PY{p}{)}
        
\PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Extracting the noisy image patches}
\PY{n}{blk\PYZus{}matrix\PYZus{}im} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{overlap\PYZus{}im2col}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{im}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{overlap}\PY{p}{)}

\PY{n}{sigma} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mf}{0.001} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}  \PYZpc{} 0.005  0.01}
\PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}min} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mf}{0.01} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} rc\PYZus{}min: minimal residual correlation before stopping pursuit}
\PY{n}{max\PYZus{}coeff} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{10} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} max\PYZus{}coeff: sparsity constraint for signal representation 10}

\PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Inpainting the Patches (OMP)}
\PY{n}{Coeff} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{OMP\PYZus{}Inpainting}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{D}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{blk\PYZus{}matrix\PYZus{}im}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{blk\PYZus{}mask}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{blk\PYZus{}mask}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{sigma}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}min}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{max\PYZus{}coeff}\PY{p}{)} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}256*146405}
\PY{n}{Coeff} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{Coeff}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{toarray}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}

\PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Creating the output image}
\PY{n}{out\PYZus{}mask} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{overlap\PYZus{}col2im}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{D}\PY{n+nd}{@Coeff}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{blk\PYZus{}mask}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{overlap}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{img\PYZus{}mask}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{)}
\PY{n}{out\PYZus{}mask} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{out\PYZus{}mask} \PY{o}{/} \PY{n}{out\PYZus{}mask}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{max}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}
\end{Verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}

    \includegraphics{images/out_OMP_inpaint.png}

    \hypertarget{image-denoising-with-sparse-representations-omp}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{4.3 Image Denoising with Sparse
Representations
(OMP)}}{4.3 Image Denoising with Sparse Representations (OMP)}}\label{image-denoising-with-sparse-representations-omp}}

Image denoising is peeformed by reconstructing each patch via sparse
coding, each patch is represented as a sparse combination of dictionary
atoms that best explain it. Noisy components that do not align with any
basis atoms are effectively removed:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Observation Model}: given a noisy image:
  \(\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{x} + \eta\) with \(x\), \(y\) and \(\eta\)
  representing the original image, degraded (noisy) image and additive
  noise, respectively.
\item
  \textbf{Patch-Based Representation}: the noisy image is decomposed
  into overlapping square patches of size \$ b \times b \$, vectorized
  as: \(\mathbf{y}_k \in \mathbb{R}^n, \quad n = b^2\). Collecting all
  patches yields:
  \(\mathbf{Y} = \begin{bmatrix} | & | & & | \ \mathbf{y}_1 & \mathbf{y}_2 & \cdots & \mathbf{y}_P \ | & | & & | \end{bmatrix} \in \mathbb{R}^{n \times P}\),
  where \(P\) is the total number of extracted patches. Define a
  patch-extraction operator \(\mathcal{R}_k\) that extracts the \(k\)-th
  patch from an image:
  \(\mathbf{y}_k = \mathcal{R}_k(y)=\mathbf{y}_k = \mathcal{R}_k(x) + \mathcal{R}_k(\eta)\).
\item
  \textbf{Sparse Representation Model}: Each noisy patch is assumed to
  admit a sparse representation over an overcomplete dictionary
  \(\mathbf{D} \in \mathbb{R}^{n \times K}\):
  \(\mathbf{y}_k = \mathbf{D}\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k + \mathbf{n}_k\)
  where:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \(\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k \in \mathbb{R}^K\) is sparse and corresponds
    to the \textbf{clean patch}
  \item
    \(\mathbf{n}_k = \mathcal{R}_k(\eta)\) represents noise
  \item
    \(\mathbf{D}\) is fixed and known
  \item
    \(K > n\),
  \end{itemize}

  making the dictionary overcomplete, where \(\mathbf{D}\) is a
  \textbf{redundant DCT dictionary}, well suited for representing local
  image structures such as edges and textures.
\item
  \textbf{Sparse Coding via Orthogonal Matching Pursuit}: The sparse
  coefficient vector \(\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k\) is estimated by solving:
  \(\underset{\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k}{\min} \|\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k\|_0 \quad \text{subject to} \quad \|\mathbf{y}_k - \mathbf{D}\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k\|_2 \le \varepsilon\),
  where \(\varepsilon\) is a noise-dependent threshold. This nonconvex
  problem is approximately solved using \textbf{Orthogonal Matching
  Pursuit (OMP) Algorithm}.
\item
  \textbf{Patch Reconstruction}: The denoised patch is reconstructed as:
  \(\hat{\mathbf{x}}_k = \mathbf{D}\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k\). Since noise
  lacks a sparse representation in the dictionary, it is largely
  excluded from the reconstruction.
\item
  \textbf{Image Reconstruction via Overlap Averaging}: Each pixel
  belongs to multiple overlapping patches. Let \(\Omega(p)\) denote the
  set of patches covering pixel \(p\). The final denoised image is
  obtained by weighted averaging:
  \(\hat{I}(p) = \frac{1}{|\Omega(p)|} \sum\limits_{k \in \Omega(p)} \hat{x}_k(p)\).
  This aggregation step further reduces residual noise due to averaging
  of uncorrelated errors.
\item
  \textbf{Extension to Color Images}: The denoising process is applied
  independently to each color channel:
  \(I^{(c)} \rightarrow \hat{I}^{(c)}, \quad c \in {R, G, B}\). This
  separable treatment simplifies implementation while maintaining
  effective noise suppression.
\item
  The described algorithm performs \textbf{nonlinear adaptive
  filtering}:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Sparse coding preserves structured image content
  \item
    Noise is rejected due to lack of sparse structure
  \item
    Overlapping patches enforce spatial consistency
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

This framework forms the foundation of several state-of-the-art methods,
including \textbf{K-SVD denoising}, \textbf{BM3D}, and
\textbf{convolutional sparse coding} approaches.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

Below is a \textbf{signal-processing / sparse-representation--centric
explanation} of how this code performs \textbf{image denoising via OMP
(Orthogonal Matching Pursuit)}. Let's try to understand it
\textbf{algorithmically}, \textbf{mathematically}, and
\textbf{line-by-line conceptually}, exactly in the spirit of
\emph{sparse land} methods (Elad--Aharon--Donoho style). The next code
snippet implements \textbf{patch-based sparse denoising}:

\begin{quote}
Each noisy image patch is assumed to be \textbf{sparsely representable}
in a \textbf{fixed dictionary} (DCT here). Noise is not sparse → OMP
naturally ignores it.
\end{quote}

\textbf{Pipeline}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Split image into \textbf{overlapping patches}
\item
  Represent each patch as
  \(\mathbf{x} = \mathbf{D}\boldsymbol{\alpha} + \mathbf{n}\)
\item
  Recover sparse coefficients \(\boldsymbol{\alpha}\) using \textbf{OMP}
\item
  Reconstruct clean patches
  \(\hat{\mathbf{x}} = \mathbf{D}\boldsymbol{\alpha}\)
\item
  Average overlapping patches back into the image.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Dictionary: Fixed DCT Basis}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{bb }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{8}
\NormalTok{K }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{16}
\NormalTok{D }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ get\_dct\_dictionary(bb, K)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Patch size: \(8 \times 8 = 64\)
\item
  Dictionary: \(\mathbf{D} \in \mathbb{R}^{64 \times 256}\)
\item
  Overcomplete DCT dictionary:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Columns = atoms
  \item
    Natural images are sparse in DCT space
  \end{itemize}
\item
  No dictionary learning here (contrast with K-SVD)
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Patch Extraction (\texttt{im2col})}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{blk\_matrix\_im }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ overlap\_im2col(im\_noisy[...,i], bb, overlap)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

This produces:
\(\mathbf{X} = \begin{bmatrix} | & | & | \ \mathbf{x}_1 & \mathbf{x}_2 & \cdots \ | & | & | \end{bmatrix} \in \mathbb{R}^{64 \times P}\)
* Each column = vectorized noisy patch * Overlapping ensures spatial
consistency

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Core Function: \texttt{OMP\_denoising}}

This is \textbf{pure OMP per patch}. \textbf{Sparse Model} For each
patch \(\mathbf{x}_k\):
\(\underset{\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k}{min} |\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k|_0 \quad \text{s.t.} \quad \|\mathbf{x}_k - \mathbf{D}\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k\|_2 \le \epsilon\)

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Initialization}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{x }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ X[:,k]}
\NormalTok{residual }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ x}
\NormalTok{indx }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ []}
\NormalTok{DD }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ []}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Residual starts as the noisy patch
  \item
    \texttt{DD} will hold \textbf{selected atoms}
  \item
    \texttt{indx} stores their indices
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{OMP Atom Selection}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{proj }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.}\BuiltInTok{abs}\NormalTok{(Dict.T }\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{ residual)}
\NormalTok{pos }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.argmax(proj)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

  Mathematically:
  \(j^\star = \arg\underset{j}{max} |\langle \mathbf{d}_j, \mathbf{r} \rangle|\)

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Choose atom most correlated with current residual
  \item
    Noise has low correlation → ignored
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Active Dictionary Update}
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{DD }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.hstack((DD, Dict[:,pos]))}
\NormalTok{indx.append(pos)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Now:
\(\mathbf{D}_{\Lambda} = [\mathbf{d}_{j_1}, \mathbf{d}_{j_2}, \dots]\)

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Orthogonal Projection (Key OMP Step)}
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{a }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ lsqr(DD, x)[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{residual }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ x }\OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ DD }\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{ a}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Solves:
\(\boldsymbol{\alpha}_\Lambda = \arg \underset{\alpha}{min} \|\mathbf{x} - \mathbf{D}_\Lambda \alpha\|_2\)

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Orthogonality} prevents atom reuse
\item
  This is why it's \emph{Orthogonal} MP
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Stopping Criteria (Very Important)}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ControlFlowTok{while}\NormalTok{ norm(residual) }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}}\NormalTok{ threshold}
      \KeywordTok{and}\NormalTok{ rc\_max }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}}\NormalTok{ rc\_min}
      \KeywordTok{and}\NormalTok{ sparsity }\OperatorTok{\textless{}}\NormalTok{ max\_coeff:}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\textbf{Three stopping rules}:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule
Criterion & Meaning \\
\midrule
\endhead
\texttt{\textbackslash{}\textbar{}\ r\ \textbackslash{}\textbar{}\ \textgreater{}\ σ}
& Stop when residual ≈ noise \\
\texttt{rc\_max\ \textgreater{}\ rc\_min} & Stop when atoms stop
correlating \\
\texttt{\#coeff\ \textless{}\ max\_coeff} & Enforce sparsity \\
\bottomrule
\end{longtable}

This is \textbf{denoising-specific OMP}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Sparse Coefficient Storage}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{A[indx, k] }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ a}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Sparse matrix \(\mathbf{A} \in \mathbb{R}^{256 \times P}\)
\item
  Each column has ≤10 non-zeros
\item
  Noise does not survive sparse projection
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Patch Reconstruction}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{D }\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{ Coeff}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Each denoised patch:
\(\hat{\mathbf{x}}_k = \mathbf{D}\boldsymbol{\alpha}_k\). This is
effectively a \textbf{nonlinear filter}:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Signal survives (sparse)
\item
  Noise rejected (dense)
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Overlap-Averaging} (\texttt{col2im})

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{overlap\_col2im(D}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{Coeff, bb, overlap, (M,N))}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\textbf{Why averaging works}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Noise is uncorrelated across patches
\item
  Signal is consistent
\item
  Averaging → variance reduction
\end{itemize}

Mathematically:
\(\hat{I}(p) = \frac{1}{|\Omega_p|} \sum\limits_{k \in \Omega_p} \hat{x}_k(p)\)

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Why This is Denoising (Not Just Reconstruction)}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule
Component & Role \\
\midrule
\endhead
Sparse constraint & Removes noise \\
DCT dictionary & Natural image prior \\
Residual threshold & Noise-aware stopping \\
Overlap averaging & Noise suppression \\
LS projection & Bias reduction \\
\bottomrule
\end{longtable}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Conceptual Interpretation}

\begin{quote}
\textbf{OMP is acting as a learned adaptive band-pass filter}
\end{quote}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Atoms selected ≈ edges, textures
\item
  High-frequency noise ≠ dictionary atoms
\item
  Sparse pursuit naturally rejects noise
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Relation to Classic Sparse Denoising}

This is essentially:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Elad \& Aharon (2006)
\item
  Starck--Elad--Donoho sparse representation denoising
\item
  Fixed dictionary variant of \textbf{K-SVD denoising}
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Under the Hood: Why Sparse Coding Works}

Sparse representations work because \textbf{natural images are highly
structured} --- edges, textures, and smooth regions can be efficiently
represented by a few DCT or wavelet atoms.

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Noise}, being random, doesn't match dictionary atoms →
  suppressed.
\item
  \textbf{Missing pixels}, through patch reconstruction, are inferred
  from similar neighboring patterns.
\end{itemize}

Thus, sparse coding inherently imposes a \emph{strong image prior},
favoring natural, piecewise-smooth reconstructions.

\textbf{Sparse representation--based denoising using OMP} relies on
three key principles:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Local image patches are sparse in suitable dictionaries
\item
  Orthogonal pursuit separates signal from noise
\item
  Overlap-averaging improves robustness and visual quality
\end{enumerate}

Together, these elements provide a powerful and interpretable approach
to image denoising grounded in sparse signal modeling.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\textbf{Results and Observations}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
Task & Method & Dictionary & Visual Outcome \\
\midrule
\endhead
Inpainting & OMP + DCT & DCT (8×8) & Clean reconstruction of masked
areas \\
Denoising & OMP + DCT & DCT (8×8) & Smooth denoised image with edge
preservation \\
Denoising & OMP + Haar & Haar (8×8) & Slightly coarser texture \\
\bottomrule
\end{longtable}

    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Initialise the matrix that stores the cubetalative signal used to calculate each pixel}
    \PY{n}{S} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{zeros}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{M}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{N}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Calculate how many patches fit horisontally and vertically}
    \PY{n}{row} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{M} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{/}\PY{o}{/}\PY{n}{overlap}
    \PY{n}{col} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{N} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{/}\PY{o}{/}\PY{n}{overlap}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Iterate through patches and keep a counter to know what column of X to access next}
    \PY{n}{counter} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{row}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{col}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:} 
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Get x and y range of current patch}
            \PY{n}{x\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{y\PYZus{}patch} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{arange}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{i}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{overlap}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{arange}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{j}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{overlap}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Get existing patch}
            \PY{n}{existing\PYZus{}patch} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{x\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{y\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Get current patch and calculate its signal strength}
            \PY{n}{current\PYZus{}patch} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{reshape}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{X}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{counter}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}signal = np.sum(Mask[:,counter]!=0)}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Update cubetalative signal strength}
            \PY{n}{S}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{x\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{y\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{+}\PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1} 
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Update patch}
            \PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{x\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{y\PYZus{}patch}\PY{p}{[}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{existing\PYZus{}patch} \PY{o}{+} \PY{n}{current\PYZus{}patch}
            \PY{n}{counter} \PY{o}{+}\PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}
    \PY{n}{S} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{S} \PY{o}{/} \PY{n}{S}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{max}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} If a pixel was not covered by a single patch with signal, set its signal}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} value to 1, in order to prevent division by zero}
    \PY{n}{S}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{S} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Divide each pixel by its corresponding cubetalative signal coverage}
    \PY{n}{I} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{I} \PY{o}{/} \PY{n}{S}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{I}

\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{OMP\PYZus{}denoising}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{D}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{X}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{sigma}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}min}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{max\PYZus{}coeff}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{orig}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{noisy}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{bb}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{KK}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{ch}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}    
    \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{P} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{X}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} 64 * 552108}
    \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{K} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{D}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}
    \PY{n}{A} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{sparse}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{D}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{X}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{k} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{P}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{n}{indx} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{]}
        \PY{n}{Dict} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{D}
        \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}W = 1/np.sqrt(np.diag(Dict.T@Dict))}
        \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}Dict = Dict@np.diag(W)}
        \PY{n}{x} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{X}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{k}\PY{p}{]} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} patch exclude mask}
        \PY{n}{residual}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{a} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{x}\PY{p}{,} \PY{k+kc}{None}
        \PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}max} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{inf}
        \PY{n}{threshold} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{linalg}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{norm}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{x}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{sigma}
        \PY{n}{DD} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{array}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)} 
        \PY{k}{while} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{linalg}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{norm}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{residual}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{n}{threshold} \PY{o+ow}{and} \PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}max} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}min} \PY{o+ow}{and} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{sum}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{a}\PY{o}{!=}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{\PYZlt{}} \PY{n}{max\PYZus{}coeff}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n}{proj} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{abs}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{Dict}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{T}\PY{n+nd}{@residual}\PY{p}{)}
            \PY{n}{pos} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{argmax}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{proj}\PY{p}{)}
            \PY{n}{rc\PYZus{}max} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{proj}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{pos}\PY{p}{]}
            \PY{n}{DD} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{Dict}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{pos}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{reshape}\PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)} \PY{k}{if} \PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{DD}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+m+mi}{0} \PY{k}{else} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{hstack}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{DD}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{Dict}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{pos}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{reshape}\PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
            \PY{n}{indx}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{append}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{pos}\PY{p}{)}
            \PY{n}{a} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{lsqr}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{DD}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{x}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}
            \PY{n}{residual} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{x} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n}{DD}\PY{n+nd}{@a}
            \PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{+}\PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}                       
        \PY{k}{if} \PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{indx}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n}{A}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{indx}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{k}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{a}
            \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}A[:,k]=W*A[:,k]            }
        \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{k} \PY{o}{\PYZpc{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{20} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n+nb}{print}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+sa}{f}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{iter:  }\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZob{}}\PY{n}{k}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZcb{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{/}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZob{}}\PY{n}{P}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZcb{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{ | (\PYZpc{}}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZob{}}\PY{n}{k}\PY{o}{/}\PY{n}{P}\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZcb{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZpc{}\PYZpc{})}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}

    \includegraphics{images/out_OMP_denoise.png}

    \hypertarget{image-colorization-with-optimization}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{5. Image Colorization with
Optimization}}{5. Image Colorization with Optimization}}\label{image-colorization-with-optimization}}

Colorization by optimization is a classical and elegant approach that
forbetalates the problem as \textbf{propagating chrominance (color)
information} from a few user-provided colored scribbles (or a source
color image) into a grayscale image, using the grayscale luminance to
guide propagation. The seminal paper by Levin, Lischinski \& Weiss
(2004) casts this as a large sparse linear system derived from a
quadratic energy; solving that system yields globally-consistent
colorization that preserves edges and texture boundaries.

\hypertarget{problem-statement-and-model}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Problem Statement and
Model}}{Problem Statement and Model}}\label{problem-statement-and-model}}

Let the input grayscale image be \(Y : \Omega \to \mathbb{R}\)
(luminance), defined on pixel domain \(\Omega\) with \(n\) pixels. We
want to estimate chrominance channels \(U\) and \(V\) (or \(I\) and
\(Q\), or \(Cb\)/\(Cr\)) so that the final color image \((Y,U,V)\) is
visually plausible. We are given a sparse set of \textbf{marked pixels}
(scribbles) where both luminance and chrominance are known
(user-specified colors). Denote the set of marked pixel indices by
\(M \subset {1,\dots,n}\). For notational simplicity, write \(u_i\) for
the chrominance value (e.g.~\(U\)) at pixel \(i\) and \(y_i\) for
luminance at pixel \(i\). The optimization principle (Levin et al.) is
to choose \(u\) that minimizes a weighted quadratic cost encouraging
each pixel's chrominance to be close to a weighted average of its
neighbors' chrominances --- i.e.~prefer smooth color except across
luminance edges:

\(E(u) = \sum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\left( u_i - \sum\limits_{j \in \mathcal{N}(i)} w_{ij} u_j \right)^2 \quad\text{subject to}\quad u_i = u_i^*,\; \forall i\in M\)

where:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \(\mathcal{N}(i)\) is a local neighborhood of pixel \(i\) (typically
  \(8\)-connected or a small window),
\item
  \(w_{ij}\) are weights expressing the affinity between pixels \(i\)
  and \(j\) based on luminance similarity (and optionally spatial
  proximity).
\end{itemize}

Intuition: if two nearby pixels have very similar luminance \(y\), they
should have similar chrominance. The weights enforce that pixels average
chrominance from ``luminance-similar'' neighbors. Fixing values on
scribbles makes the linear system well-posed.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{weight-design}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Weight
Design}}{Weight Design}}\label{weight-design}}

A common weight definition is:
\(w_{ij} = \exp\Big(-\frac{(y_i - y_j)^2}{\sigma_i^2}\Big)\) where
\(\sigma_i\) is a local scale (e.g.~standard deviation of luminance in
the neighborhood of \(i\)). Often these weights are normalized so that
the off-diagonal entries sum to \(1\) (and diagonal is set to \(1\) in
the linear system formulation). Levin et al.~use a slightly different
but equivalent construction --- the code implements weights that end up
forming a sparse matrix \(W\) such that:
\(W_{ii} = 1, \quad W_{ij} = -\frac{w_{ij}}{\sum_{k\in\mathcal{N}(i)} w_{ik}}, \quad j\in\mathcal{N}(i)\),
so that the energy is \(u^T W u\) (up to a constant) and the solution
for unknown chrominance values is found by solving a sparse linear
system.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{discrete-linear-system}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Discrete Linear
System}}{Discrete Linear System}}\label{discrete-linear-system}}

Partition the unknown vector \(u\) into unknowns and knowns (scribbles).
The Euler--Lagrange optimality condition for the quadratic energy gives
a linear system: \(Wu = b\), where \(W\) is large, symmetric (in
practice sparse, diagonally dominant) and \(b\) encodes the fixed
chrominance values: rows corresponding to marked pixels enforce
\(u_i = u_i^*\), and rows for unmarked pixels contain the
\(\sum w_{ij} u_j\) terms rearranged. In the next demonstration code,
the matrix \(W\) is constructed so that solving \(W u = U_{\text{vec}}\)
(where \(U_{\text{vec}}\) encodes the marked values and zeros elsewhere)
yields the completed chrominance channel. Since the energy is quadratic
and convex, standard sparse linear solvers (Cholesky, sparse LU,
conjugate gradient) obtain the global minimizer.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{overall-algorithm}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Overall
Algorithm}}{Overall Algorithm}}\label{overall-algorithm}}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Convert the input RGB image to a luminance/chrominance color space
  (\(YUV\) or \(YIQ\)). Keep luminance (\(Y\)) fixed.
\item
  Identify marked pixels \(M\) from the user-marked image (pixels where
  the user provided chrominance).
\item
  For each unmarked pixel \(i\), compute neighbors \(\mathcal{N}(i)\)
  and weights \(w_{ij}\) based on luminance differences (and optionally
  spatial distance).
\item
  Assemble sparse matrix \(W\) such that \(W_{ii}=1\) and
  \(W_{ij}=-w_{ij}/\sum w_{ik}\) for neighbors.
\item
  Form the right-hand side vector(s) from the chrominance values at
  marked pixels.
\item
  Solve the sparse linear system for each chrominance channel \(U\) and
  \(V\) independently.
\item
  Combine \(Y\) with solved \(U\),\(V\) and invert color transform to
  \(RGB\).
\end{enumerate}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{demonstration-with-python-code}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Demonstration with python
code}}{Demonstration with python code}}\label{demonstration-with-python-code}}

Refer to the next code snippet for python demonstration, first let's
import the required libraries and define a few helper functions:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  The helper function \texttt{rgb2yuv()} converts RGB to YUV-like
  channels. Channel 0 is luminance (Y), channels 1--2 are chrominance
  (U,V). You can also use YIQ (functions below) --- the idea is to fix Y
  and solve for chrominance channels.
\item
  The function \texttt{yuv2rgb()} implements the inverse transform back
  to RGB.
\end{itemize}

    \begin{tcolorbox}[breakable, size=fbox, boxrule=1pt, pad at break*=1mm,colback=cellbackground, colframe=cellborder]

    \PY{n}{rgb}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{yuv}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{+} \PY{l+m+mf}{1.13983}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{yuv}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{]}

    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}rgb = rgb.astype(np.uint8)}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}plt.imshow(rgb); plt.show();}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{rgb}

\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{rgb2yiq}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{rgb}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}

    \hypertarget{neighborhood-and-helpers}{%
\paragraph{Neighborhood and helpers:}\label{neighborhood-and-helpers}}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  The function \texttt{get\_nbrs()}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Returns an 8-connected neighborhood of pixel ((x,y)).
  \item
    Also computes local standard deviation of luminance over pixel and
    its neighbors. That local scale (\sigma) is used later to normalize
    weight exponent.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \texttt{neighborhood} and \texttt{ij2id} are helper utilities:
  \texttt{ij2id} maps 2D indices to 1D index for sparse matrix assembly.
\end{itemize}

    \begin{tcolorbox}[breakable, size=fbox, boxrule=1pt, pad at break*=1mm,colback=cellbackground, colframe=cellborder]

    \hypertarget{weight-matrix-assembly}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Weight matrix
assembly}}{Weight matrix assembly}}\label{weight-matrix-assembly}}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{compute\_W(Y,\ colored)}: This is the core of the algorithm:
  building the sparse matrix \(W\).
\item
  Key steps:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Loop over all pixels \((i,j)\) not in the set \texttt{colored}
    (pixels with unknown chrominance).
  \item
    For each pixel:

    \begin{itemize}
    \tightlist
    \item
      Get neighbors \(N\) and local sigma from \texttt{get\_nbrs}.
    \item
      For each neighbor \(s\in N\), set a provisional weight
      \(w_{is} = e^{-(Y_i - Y_s)^2 / \sigma^2}\) if \(\sigma>0\).
    \item
      Let \(Z = \sum\limits_{s\in N} w_{is}\). Then normalized
      off-diagonal entries become \(W_{is} = -w_{is}/Z\). The diagonal
      is set to \(W_{ii}=1\).
    \end{itemize}
  \item
    For marked pixels, the code will still set \(W_{ii}=1\) (so the
    linear system enforces equality).
  \item
    The result is a sparse matrix \texttt{W} of size \(n\times n\)
    (where \texttt{n\ =\ w*h})), assembled as a
    \texttt{scipy.sparse.csc\_matrix}. This corresponds to the discrete
    operator in the quadratic energy described earlier.
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Notes on the sign and normalization}: The code writes
off-diagonals as negative and diagonal as +1 so that each row enforces
\(u_i - \sum_{j} \lambda_{ij} u_j = b_i\). For unmarked pixels
\(b_i=0\); for marked pixels \(b_i=u_i^*\) (this is handled by placing
marked values into the right-hand vector and solving).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{marked-locations}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Marked
locations}}{Marked locations}}\label{marked-locations}}

In the function \texttt{find\_marked\_locations()}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{bw} is the base grayscale image in the chosen color space (or
  a representation without scribbles), and \texttt{marked} is the image
  where the scribbles (user-provided colors) are present.
\item
  The difference identifies pixels where chrominance channels were
  changed (i.e.~locations with user color).
\item
  Return a set of coordinates that are ``\textbf{colored}'' --- these
  pixels are constrained in the linear system.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{solving-for-chrominance-colorize_optyuv-yuvm}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Solving for chrominance ---
\texttt{colorize\_opt(yuv,\ yuvm)}}}{Solving for chrominance --- colorize\_opt(yuv, yuvm)}}\label{solving-for-chrominance-colorize_optyuv-yuvm}}

High-level steps in \texttt{colorize\_opt}:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{Y\ =\ yuv{[}:,:,0{]}} extracts luminance.
\item
  \texttt{colored\ =\ find\_marked\_locations(yuv,\ yuvm)} identifies
  scribbled pixels.
\item
  \texttt{W\ =\ compute\_W(Y,\ colored)} builds the sparse matrix.
\item
  Extract vectors \(U\) and \(V\) from the marked color image
  \texttt{yuvm} (these vectors contain both zeros for unknown locations
  and the user-provided chrominance at marked locations).
\item
  Solve the linear systems:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \texttt{W\ *\ U\_complete\ =\ U\_vec}
  \item
    \texttt{W\ *\ V\_complete\ =\ V\_vec} The code uses
    \texttt{LU\ =\ sp.linalg.splu(W)} and \texttt{LU.solve(U\_vec)}
    (sparse LU) to get solutions.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  Reassemble \texttt{sol} which contains (Y) (unchanged) and computed
  chrominance channels \texttt{U1,V1}.
\item
  Convert back to RGB with \texttt{yiq2rgb} (or \texttt{yuv2rgb}) and
  display.
\end{enumerate}

This exactly implements the discrete minimization of the quadratic
energy with \textbf{Dirichlet boundary conditions} (fixed scribble
values).

    \begin{tcolorbox}[breakable, size=fbox, boxrule=1pt, pad at break*=1mm,colback=cellbackground, colframe=cellborder]
\prompt{In}{incolor}{40}{\boxspacing}
\begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{find\PYZus{}marked\PYZus{}locations}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{bw}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{marked}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
    \PY{n}{diff} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{marked} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n}{bw}
    \PY{n}{colored} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{n+nb}{set}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n+nb}{zip}\PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{nonzero}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{diff}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)} \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{colored}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{union}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{colored}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}

\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{sum\PYZus{}sqr\PYZus{}dist}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{U}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{W}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
    \PY{n}{sum\PYZus{}sqr} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{r} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{U}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{n}{x}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{y} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{r} \PY{o}{\PYZpc{}} \PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{r} \PY{o}{/} \PY{n}{h}
        \PY{n}{nbrs}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{\PYZus{}} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{get\PYZus{}nbrs}\PY{p}{(}\PY{k+kc}{None}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{x}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{y}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)} 
        \PY{n}{sum\PYZus{}sqr} \PY{o}{+}\PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{U}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{r}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n+nb}{sum}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{W}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{x}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{y}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{x1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{y1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{U}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{w}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{x1}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{y1}\PY{p}{]} \PY{k}{for} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{x1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{y1}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n}{nbrs}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{*}\PY{o}{*}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{sum\PYZus{}sqr}	

\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{compute\PYZus{}W}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{Y}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{colored}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
    \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{Y}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}	
    \PY{n}{W} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{defaultdict}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{k}{if} \PY{o+ow}{not} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n}{colored}\PY{p}{:}
                \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{N}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{sigma}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{get\PYZus{}nbrs}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{Y}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}r = (i, j)}
                \PY{n}{Z} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mf}{0.}
                \PY{n}{id1} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{ij2id}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)}
                \PY{k}{for} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{i1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j1}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n}{N}\PY{p}{:} 					 \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}s = (i1, j1)}
                    \PY{n}{id2} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{ij2id}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{i1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)}
                    \PY{n}{W}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{id1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{id2}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{exp}\PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{Y}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{n}{Y}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{*}\PY{o}{*}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{o}{/}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{sigma}\PY{o}{*}\PY{o}{*}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)} \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{sigma} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{0} \PY{k}{else} \PY{l+m+mf}{0.}

                \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{Z} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{:}	
                    \PY{k}{for} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{i1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j1}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n}{N}\PY{p}{:} 				 \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}s = (i1, j1)}
                        \PY{n}{id2} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{ij2id}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{i1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)}
                        \PY{n}{W}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{id1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{id2}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{/}\PY{o}{=} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{n}{Z}
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n+nb}{id} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{ij2id}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{w}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)}
            \PY{n}{W}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n+nb}{id}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n+nb}{id}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mf}{1.}
    \PY{n}{rows}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{cols} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n+nb}{zip}\PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{*}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{W}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{keys}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}keys}
    \PY{n}{data} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n+nb}{list}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{W}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{values}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}[W[k] for k in keys]}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{sp}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{csc\PYZus{}matrix}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{data}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n+nb}{list}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{rows}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n+nb}{list}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{cols}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{shape}\PY{o}{=}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{w}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{w}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{h}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}W}

\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{colorize\PYZus{}opt}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{yuv}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{yuvm}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
    \PY{n}{Y} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{yuv}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}
    \PY{n}{colored} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{find\PYZus{}marked\PYZus{}locations}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{yuv}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{yuvm}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{n}{W} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{compute\PYZus{}W}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{Y}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{colored}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{n}{U}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{V} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{yuvm}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{yuvm}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{]}
    \PY{n}{U\PYZus{}vec}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{V\PYZus{}vec} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{U}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{ravel}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{V}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{ravel}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}

    \PY{n}{sol}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{Y}
    \PY{n}{U1} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{LU}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{solve}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{U\PYZus{}vec}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{reshape}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{U}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{U}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{n}{V1} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{LU}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{solve}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{V\PYZus{}vec}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{reshape}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{V}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{V}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}U1[U1 \PYZlt{} 0], V1[V1 \PYZlt{} 0] = 0., 0.}
    \PY{n}{sol}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{U1}
    \PY{n}{sol}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{V1}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{sol}

\PY{n}{imfile} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{images/waterfall\PYZus{}gray.png}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}

\PY{n}{rgb\PYZus{}colorized}  \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{yiq2rgb}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{yuv\PYZus{}colorized}\PY{p}{)}

\PY{n}{plt}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{figure}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{figsize}\PY{o}{=}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+m+mi}{15}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{7}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}

    \begin{center}
    \adjustimage{max size={0.9\linewidth}{0.9\paperheight}}{Chapter3_files/Chapter3_52_0.png}
    \end{center}
    { \hspace*{\fill} \\}
    
    \hypertarget{numerical-and-implementation-notes}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Numerical and implementation
notes}}{Numerical and implementation notes}}\label{numerical-and-implementation-notes}}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Sigma (local scale)}: If a neighborhood has zero variance
  (constant luminance), the code uses sigma=0 and sets weights to zero;
  this can make the denominator (Z) zero --- the code checks
  \texttt{if\ Z\textgreater{}0} before normalizing. In practice one uses
  a small constant (\sigma\_\{\min\}) to prevent division by zero.
\item
  \textbf{Normalization and sign}: The matrix is constructed so that
  rows corresponding to unknown pixels enforce the averaging constraint;
  rows for scribbled pixels enforce equality.
\item
  \textbf{Sparse linear solve}: \texttt{splu} factorization is efficient
  for repeated solves (here we solve once per channel). For very large
  images, iterative solvers (conjugate gradient with preconditioning)
  may be faster.
\item
  \textbf{Boundary handling}: Neighborhood is 8-connected; you could
  include a larger window (e.g., 5×5) with spatial weighting.
\item
  \textbf{Color-space scaling}: If using RGB in {[}0,255{]}, be
  consistent; many formulations expect normalized {[}0,1{]} luminance.
  The code mixes normalizations; ensure inputs are scaled consistently.
\item
  \textbf{Stability}: For very sparse scribbles, matrix (W) can be
  ill-conditioned. Adding a tiny diagonal regularizer (\varepsilon I) or
  smoothing the luminance first helps.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{practical-improvements-modern-remarks}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Practical improvements \& modern
remarks}}{Practical improvements \& modern remarks}}\label{practical-improvements-modern-remarks}}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Window-based affinities}: Instead of only 8 neighbors, using a
  patch window and computing affinities between the central pixel and
  all pixels in the window improves color bleeding across textured
  regions (this is used in some variants).
\item
  \textbf{multi-scale propagation}: Solve at coarse-to-fine scales to
  better propagate color over long distances.
\item
  \textbf{Regularization}: Add a small Tikhonov term to (W) (i.e.~(W +
  \lambda I)) if the system is poorly conditioned.
\item
  \textbf{Learning-based colorization}: Recent deep-learning methods
  (e.g., CNN-based colorization) produce more semantic colors, but
  optimization propagation remains useful for interactive, controllable
  colorization and for small scribble-driven edits.
\item
  \textbf{Performance}: Build \texttt{W} with vectorized sparse assembly
  instead of Python loops for speed; use \texttt{numba} or C extensions
  for very large images.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{demonstration-code-mapping-to-math}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Demonstration code mapping to
math}}{Demonstration code mapping to math}}\label{demonstration-code-mapping-to-math}}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{Y} ← luminance (kept fixed).
\item
  \texttt{W} ← sparse matrix built from pixel affinities (weights).
\item
  Solve \texttt{W\ *\ U\_vec\ =\ U\_marked} and
  \texttt{W\ *\ V\_vec\ =\ V\_marked}.
\item
  \texttt{sol} ← reconstructed YUV (or YIQ), convert to RGB.
\end{itemize}

This yields the global minimizer of the quadratic energy with Dirichlet
constraints on marked pixels.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{notes}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Notes}}{Notes}}\label{notes}}

The implementation already embodies the Levin et al.~approach and will
work well for moderate-sized images and reasonably distributed
scribbles. A few practical suggestions to make it more robust:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Fix \texttt{norm} function} if used (it had an operator
  precedence bug in earlier snippets). Use the safe normalization
  function shown above.
\item
  \textbf{Guard sigma}: in \texttt{get\_nbrs}, if computed
  \texttt{sigma} is very small, set \texttt{sigma\ =\ max(sigma,\ 1e-6)}
  to avoid division by zero.
\item
  \textbf{Vectorize \texttt{compute\_W}} building: the double
  \texttt{for} loops are simple but slow for large images; consider
  assembling data/row/col lists and creating the sparse matrix in one
  shot (the code does that but still loops to compute values).
\item
  \textbf{Use iterative solver} if the image is large:
  \texttt{scipy.sparse.linalg.cg} or \texttt{minres} with an incomplete
  LU preconditioner may be faster.
\item
  \textbf{Post-clamp colors}: after solving, clip chrominance channels
  to expected ranges before converting to RGB.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{figure-layout}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Figure
layout}}{Figure layout}}\label{figure-layout}}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Left: original grayscale input (Y).
\item
  Middle: marked image (user scribbles).
\item
  Right: colorized output obtained by solving the sparse linear system
  and converting back to RGB.
\end{itemize}

This demonstrates how a few colored strokes produce a
globally-consistent colored image.

    \hypertarget{optimization-in-image-resizing-and-synthesis}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{6. Optimization in Image Resizing
and
Synthesis}}{6. Optimization in Image Resizing and Synthesis}}\label{optimization-in-image-resizing-and-synthesis}}

\textbf{Content-aware Image Resizing} and \textbf{Image Synthesis} can
be naturally posed as energy minimization problems, where visual
saliency, structural continuity, and perceptual consistency are
explicitly encoded through objective functions. By optimizing these
criteria, techniques such as seam carving and image quilting produce
visually coherent resizing and realistic texture generation that go far
beyond uniform geometric scaling.

\hypertarget{seam-carving-context-aware-image-resizing-retargeting-and-object-removal}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{6.1 Seam Carving -- Context Aware
Image Resizing, Retargeting and Object
Removal}}{6.1 Seam Carving -- Context Aware Image Resizing, Retargeting and Object Removal}}\label{seam-carving-context-aware-image-resizing-retargeting-and-object-removal}}

Traditional image resizing methods such as (uniform) scaling or cropping
treat all pixels equally, often resulting in distortion of semantically
important regions (e.g., faces, objects, or edges) or removing crucial
visual content. \textbf{Seam Carving}, introduced by \textbf{Avidan and
Shamir (2007)}, provides a \textbf{content-aware image retargeting}
technique that preserves visually significant areas (e.g., objects or
edges) while adaptively removing or inserting pixels along paths of
least visual importance. Seam carving is grounded in \textbf{energy
minimization and dynamic programming}, allowing the image to be resized
while preserving perceptually salient structures. The goal of seam
carving is to reduce or expand image dimensions by modifying pixel
connectivity while minimizing perceptual distortion. Beyond resizing,
the same framework naturally extends to \textbf{object removal},
\textbf{object protection}, and \textbf{non-uniform retargeting}.

\hypertarget{dual-gradient-energy-function-measuring-pixel-importance}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Dual-Gradient Energy Function:
Measuring Pixel
Importance}}{Dual-Gradient Energy Function: Measuring Pixel Importance}}\label{dual-gradient-energy-function-measuring-pixel-importance}}

A key component of seam carving is an \textbf{energy function} that
assigns a cost to each pixel. Pixels with high energy correspond to
visually important structures. The most common choice is the
\textbf{dual-gradient energy function}:
\(E(i,j) = \left\lVert \frac{\partial \mathbf{I}}{\partial x}(i,j) \right\rVert_1 + \left\lVert \frac{\partial \mathbf{I}}{\partial y}(i,j) \right\rVert_1\),
where the gradients are approximated by finite differences. The function
\texttt{compute\_energy()}, as shown in the next code snippet implements
this function. Padding simplifies boundary handling. The \(\ell_1\)-norm
across color channels yields a scalar energy map.

    \begin{tcolorbox}[breakable, size=fbox, boxrule=1pt, pad at break*=1mm,colback=cellbackground, colframe=cellborder]
\prompt{In}{incolor}{ }{\boxspacing}
\begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{compute\PYZus{}energy}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{u}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
    \PY{n}{u1} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{zeros}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{m}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{n}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{n}{u1}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{u}
    \PY{n}{u\PYZus{}x} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{u1}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n}{u1}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}
    \PY{n}{u\PYZus{}y} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{u1}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{n}{u1}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{o}{+}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}
    \PY{n}{d\PYZus{}x} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{sum}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n+nb}{abs}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{u\PYZus{}x}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{axis}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{n}{d\PYZus{}y} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{sum}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n+nb}{abs}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{u\PYZus{}y}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{axis}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{d\PYZus{}x} \PY{o}{+} \PY{n}{d\PYZus{}y}	
\end{Verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}

    \hypertarget{seam-definition}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Seam
Definition}}{Seam Definition}}\label{seam-definition}}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{vertical-seam}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Vertical
Seam}}{Vertical Seam}}\label{vertical-seam}}

A \textbf{vertical seam} is an \(8\)-connected path from top to bottom:
\(\mathcal{S} = {(i, j_i)}_{i=1}^{m} \quad \text{such that} \quad |j_i - j_{i-1}| \le 1\).
The total seam energy is:
\(E(\mathcal{S}) = \sum\limits_{i=1}^{m} E(i, j_i)\)

\hypertarget{horizontal-seam}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Horizontal
Seam}}{Horizontal Seam}}\label{horizontal-seam}}

Similarly, a \textbf{horizontal seam} spans left to right:
\(\mathcal{S} = {(i_j, j)}_{j=1}^{n} \quad \text{with} \quad |i_j - i_{j-1}| \le 1\)

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{optimal-seam-via-dynamic-programming}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Optimal Seam via Dynamic
Programming}}{Optimal Seam via Dynamic Programming}}\label{optimal-seam-via-dynamic-programming}}

Finding the minimum-energy seam is a shortest-path problem on a directed
acyclic graph.

\hypertarget{vertical-seam-recurrence}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Vertical Seam
Recurrence}}{Vertical Seam Recurrence}}\label{vertical-seam-recurrence}}

Define the cumulative cost:
\(C(i,j) = E(i,j) + \min \begin{cases} C(i-1, j-1) \\ C(i-1, j) \\ C(i-1, j+1) \end{cases}\)

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{code-correspondence-vertical_seam_carve}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Code Correspondence:}
\texttt{vertical\_seam\_carve}}{Code Correspondence: vertical\_seam\_carve}}\label{code-correspondence-vertical_seam_carve}}

The next code snippet implements the Dynamic Program (DP) to solve the
above recurrence in a bottom-up manner efficiently. The backtracking
matrix \texttt{B} is used to find the optimal seam.

    \begin{tcolorbox}[breakable, size=fbox, boxrule=1pt, pad at break*=1mm,colback=cellbackground, colframe=cellborder]
\prompt{In}{incolor}{ }{\boxspacing}
\begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{vertical\PYZus{}seam\PYZus{}carve}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{E}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
    \PY{n}{C}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{B} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0} \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{\PYZus{}} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]} \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{\PYZus{}} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}} \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{\PYZus{}} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]} \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{\PYZus{}} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]} 
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{n}{C}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{E}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]}
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n}{minc}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{mind} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{C}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{U}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}
            \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{0} \PY{o+ow}{and} \PY{n}{C}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{\PYZlt{}} \PY{n}{minc}\PY{p}{:}
                \PY{n}{minc}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{mind} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{C}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{L}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}
            \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{\PYZlt{}} \PY{n}{n} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1} \PY{o+ow}{and} \PY{n}{C}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{+} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{\PYZlt{}} \PY{n}{minc}\PY{p}{:}
                \PY{n}{minc}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{mind} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{C}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{+} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{R}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}			
            \PY{n}{C}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{B}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{minc} \PY{o}{+} \PY{n}{E}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{mind}

    \PY{n}{seam} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{]}
    \PY{n}{min\PYZus{}c}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{min\PYZus{}j} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n+nb}{min}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{C}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{m}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{)} \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{m} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{min\PYZus{}j}
    \PY{k}{while} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}}\PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{n}{seam}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{append}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
        \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{B}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{L}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}
        \PY{k}{elif} \PY{n}{B}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{R}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n}{j} \PY{o}{+}\PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}
        \PY{n}{i} \PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{seam}	
\end{Verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}

\end{tcolorbox}

    \hypertarget{seam-removal-image-resizing}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Seam Removal: Image
Resizing}}{Seam Removal: Image Resizing}}\label{seam-removal-image-resizing}}

\hypertarget{vertical-seam-removal}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Vertical Seam
Removal}}{Vertical Seam Removal}}\label{vertical-seam-removal}}

Removing a seam deletes one pixel per row, reducing width by one:

\(\mathbf{I}'(i,j) = \begin{cases} \mathbf{I}(i,j) & j < j_i \\ \mathbf{I}(i,j+1) & j \ge j_i \end{cases}\)

The function \texttt{remove\_vertical\_seam()} in the next code snippet
implements the above, pixels to the right are shifted left.

\hypertarget{horizontal-seam-removal}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Horizontal Seam
Removal}}{Horizontal Seam Removal}}\label{horizontal-seam-removal}}

The process is identical, applied column-wise instead of row-wise,
implemented with the function \texttt{horizontal\_seam\_carve()}. This
function is the transpose-analogue of vertical seam carving.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{iterative-seam-removal-image-retargeting}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Iterative Seam Removal (Image
Retargeting)}}{Iterative Seam Removal (Image Retargeting)}}\label{iterative-seam-removal-image-retargeting}}

To reduce width by \(k\) pixels:
\(\mathbf{I}^{(k)} = \underbrace{\mathcal{R} \circ \mathcal{R} \circ \cdots \circ \mathcal{R}}_{k\ \text{times}}(\mathbf{I})\),
this is implemented using the function
\texttt{seam\_carve\_remove\_seams()}. Each iteration recomputes energy,
ensuring adaptivity.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

    \begin{tcolorbox}[breakable, size=fbox, boxrule=1pt, pad at break*=1mm,colback=cellbackground, colframe=cellborder]
\prompt{In}{incolor}{32}{\boxspacing}
\begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{remove\PYZus{}vertical\PYZus{}seam}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{vseam}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}	
    \PY{k}{for} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n}{vseam}\PY{p}{:}
        \PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{:}\PY{n}{n}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{j}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}
    \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{n}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{n}{n}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{]}

\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{seam\PYZus{}carving\PYZus{}remove\PYZus{}vertical\PYZus{}seam}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
    \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{I}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}
    \PY{n}{E} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{compute\PYZus{}energy}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{)}
    \PY{n}{vseam} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{vertical\PYZus{}seam\PYZus{}carve}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{m}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{n}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{E}\PY{p}{)}

    \hypertarget{visualization-and-interpretation}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Visualization and
Interpretation}}{Visualization and Interpretation}}\label{visualization-and-interpretation}}

The plotting functions (\texttt{plot\_energy\_seam\_removed()} and
\texttt{plot\_vertical\_seams\_removed()}) provided in the above and
below code, respectively:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Overlay seams
\item
  Display energy maps
\item
  Show before/after results
\end{itemize}

These are crucial for understanding seam behavior.

    \begin{center}

    { \hspace*{\fill} \\}
    
    \hypertarget{seam-insertion-image-enlargement}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Seam Insertion (Image
Enlargement)}}{Seam Insertion (Image Enlargement)}}\label{seam-insertion-image-enlargement}}

Seam insertion is the inverse operation:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Compute low-energy seams
\item
  Duplicate or interpolate pixels along seams
\item
  Insert seams back in reverse order
\end{enumerate}

Although not explicitly implemented here, the plotting function
reconstructs seam locations to illustrate the concept.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\hypertarget{object-removal-via-seam-carving}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Object Removal via Seam
Carving}}{Object Removal via Seam Carving}}\label{object-removal-via-seam-carving}}

\hypertarget{energy-manipulation-with-masks}{%
\paragraph{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{Energy Manipulation with
Masks}}{Energy Manipulation with Masks}}\label{energy-manipulation-with-masks}}

To remove an object, pixels belonging to the object are assigned
\textbf{large negative energy}, forcing seams to pass through them. This
is implemented with the mask \(M\): \(E'(i,j) = E(i,j) \cdot M(i,j)\).
Negative values attract seams, enabling object removal, as demonstrated
with the function \texttt{seam\_carve\_remove\_seams\_with\_mask()}
below. Repeated seam removal eliminates the masked region.

    \begin{tcolorbox}[breakable, size=fbox, boxrule=1pt, pad at break*=1mm,colback=cellbackground, colframe=cellborder]
\prompt{In}{incolor}{279}{\boxspacing}
\begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
\PY{k}{def}\PY{+w}{ }\PY{n+nf}{seam\PYZus{}carving\PYZus{}remove\PYZus{}vertical\PYZus{}seam\PYZus{}with\PYZus{}mask}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{I}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{M}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
